     7	/// Returns a list of patterns not covered by the match expression.
     8	pub fn missing_patterns(
     9	    result: &CompileCaseResult,
    10	    environment: &Environment<'_>,
    11	) -> Vec<EcoString> {
    12	    let subjects = &result.compiled_case.subject_variables;
    13	    let mut generator = MissingPatternsGenerator::new(subjects, environment);
    14	    generator.add_missing_patterns(&result.compiled_case.tree);
    15	
    16	    generator.missing.into_iter().collect()
    17	}

    20	pub struct VariantField {
    21	    pub label: Option<EcoString>,
    22	    pub variable: Variable,
    23	}
    24	
    25	/// Information about a single constructor/value (aka term) being tested, used
    26	/// to build a list of names of missing patterns.
    27	#[derive(Debug)]
    28	pub enum Term {
    29	    Variant {
    30	        variable: Variable,
    31	        name: EcoString,
    32	        module: EcoString,
    33	        fields: Vec<VariantField>,
    34	    },
    35	    Tuple {

    38	    },

    41	    },

    49	    },

    53	    pub fn variable(&self) -> &Variable {
    54	        match self {
    55	            Term::Variant { variable, .. } => variable,
    56	            Term::Tuple { variable, .. } => variable,
    57	            Term::Infinite { variable } => variable,
    58	            Term::EmptyList { variable } => variable,
    59	            Term::List { variable, .. } => variable,
    60	        }
    61	    }
    62	}

    71	
    72	impl<'a, 'env> MissingPatternsGenerator<'a, 'env> {
    73	    fn new(subjects: &'a Vec<Variable>, environment: &'a Environment<'env>) -> Self {
    74	        MissingPatternsGenerator {
    75	            subjects,
    76	            terms: vec![],
    77	            missing: IndexSet::new(),
    78	            environment,
    79	            printer: Printer::new(environment.current_module.clone(), &environment.names),
    80	        }
    81	    }
    82	
    83	    fn print_terms(&self, mapping: HashMap<usize, usize>) -> EcoString {
    84	        self.printer
    85	            .print_terms(self.subjects, &self.terms, &mapping)
    86	    }
    87	
    88	    fn add_missing_patterns(&mut self, node: &Decision) {
    89	        match node {
    90	            Decision::Run { .. } => {}
    91	
    92	            Decision::Guard { if_false, .. } => self.add_missing_patterns(if_false),
    93	
    94	            Decision::Fail => {
    95	                // At this point the terms stack looks something like this:
    96	                // `[term, term + arguments, term, ...]`. To construct a pattern
    97	                // name from this stack, we first map all variables to their
    98	                // term indexes. This is needed because when a term defines
    99	                // arguments, the terms for those arguments don't necessarily
   100	                // appear in order in the term stack.
   101	                //
   102	                // This mapping is then used when (recursively) generating a
   103	                // pattern name.
   104	                //
   105	                // This approach could probably be done more efficiently, so if
   106	                // you're reading this and happen to know of a way, please
   107	                // submit a merge request :)
   108	                let mut mapping = HashMap::new();
   109	                for (index, step) in self.terms.iter().enumerate() {
   110	                    _ = mapping.insert(step.variable().id, index);
   111	                }
   112	                let pattern = self.print_terms(mapping);
   113	
   114	                _ = self.missing.insert(pattern);
   115	            }
   116	
   117	            Decision::Switch {
   118	                var,
   119	                choices,
   120	                fallback,
   121	                fallback_check,
   122	            } => {
   123	                for (check, body) in choices {
   124	                    self.add_missing_patterns_after_check(var, check, body);
   125	                }
   126	
   127	                match fallback_check.as_ref() {
   128	                    FallbackCheck::InfiniteCatchAll => {
   129	                        self.add_missing_patterns(fallback);
   130	                    }
   131	                    FallbackCheck::RuntimeCheck { check } => {
   132	                        self.add_missing_patterns_after_check(var, check, fallback)
   133	                    }
   134	                    FallbackCheck::CatchAll { ignored_checks } => {
   135	                        for check in ignored_checks {
   136	                            self.add_missing_patterns_after_check(var, check, fallback);
   137	                        }
   138	                    }
   139	                };
   140	            }
   141	        }
   142	    }
   143	
   144	    fn add_missing_patterns_after_check(
   145	        &mut self,
   146	        var: &Variable,
   147	        check: &RuntimeCheck,
   148	        body: &Decision,
   149	    ) {
   150	        let term = self.check_to_term(var.clone(), check);
   151	        self.terms.push(term);
   152	        self.add_missing_patterns(body);
   153	        _ = self.terms.pop();
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    fn check_to_term(&self, variable: Variable, check: &RuntimeCheck) -> Term {
   157	        match check {
   158	            RuntimeCheck::Int { .. }
   159	            | RuntimeCheck::Float { .. }
   160	            | RuntimeCheck::String { .. }
   161	            | RuntimeCheck::BitArray { .. }
   162	            | RuntimeCheck::StringPrefix { .. } => Term::Infinite { variable },
   163	
   164	            RuntimeCheck::Tuple { elements, .. } => Term::Tuple {
   165	                variable,
   166	                elements: elements.clone(),
   167	            },
   168	
   169	            RuntimeCheck::Variant {
   170	                index,
   171	                fields,
   172	                labels,
   173	                ..
   174	            } => {
   175	                let (module, name) = variable
   176	                    .type_
   177	                    .named_type_name()
   178	                    .expect("Should be a named type");
   179	
   180	                let name = self
   181	                    .environment
   182	                    .get_constructors_for_type(&module, &name)
   183	                    .expect("Custom type constructor must have custom type kind")
   184	                    .variants
   185	                    .get(*index)
   186	                    .expect("Custom type constructor exist for type")
   187	                    .name
   188	                    .clone();
   189	
   190	                let fields = fields
   191	                    .iter()
   192	                    .enumerate()
   193	                    .map(|(index, variable)| VariantField {
   194	                        label: labels.get(&index).cloned(),
   195	                        variable: variable.clone(),
   196	                    })
   197	                    .collect();
   198	
   199	                Term::Variant {
   200	                    variable,
   201	                    name,
   202	                    module,
   203	                    fields,
   204	                }
   205	            }
   206	
   207	            RuntimeCheck::NonEmptyList { first, rest } => Term::List {
   208	                variable,
   209	                first: first.clone(),
   210	                rest: rest.clone(),
   211	            },
   212	
   213	            RuntimeCheck::EmptyList => Term::EmptyList { variable },
   214	        }
   215	    }
   216	}
   217

     1	use std::collections::HashMap;
     2	
     3	use ecow::EcoString;
     4	
     5	use crate::{
     6	    ast::Publicity,
     7	    type_::printer::{NameContextInformation, Names},
     8	};
     9	
    10	use super::{Variable, missing_patterns::Term};
    11	
    12	#[derive(Debug)]
    13	pub struct Printer<'a> {
    14	    names: &'a Names,
    15	    /// This is the module that is being currently analysed.
    16	    current_module: EcoString,
    17	}
    18	
    19	impl<'a> Printer<'a> {
    20	    pub fn new(current_module: EcoString, names: &'a Names) -> Self {
    21	        Printer {
    22	            current_module,
    23	            names,
    24	        }
    25	    }
    26	
    27	    pub fn print_terms(
    28	        &self,
    29	        subjects: &[Variable],
    30	        terms: &[Term],
    31	        mapping: &HashMap<usize, usize>,
    32	    ) -> EcoString {
    33	        let mut buffer = EcoString::new();
    34	        for (i, subject) in subjects.iter().enumerate() {
    35	            if i != 0 {
    36	                buffer.push_str(", ");
    37	            }
    38	
    39	            match mapping.get(&subject.id) {
    40	                Some(&index) => {
    41	                    let term = terms.get(index).expect("Term must exist");
    42	                    self.print(term, terms, mapping, &mut buffer);
    43	                }
    44	                None => buffer.push('_'),
    45	            }
    46	        }
    47	        buffer
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    fn print(
    51	        &self,
    52	        term: &Term,
    53	        terms: &[Term],
    54	        mapping: &HashMap<usize, usize>,
    55	        buffer: &mut EcoString,
    56	    ) {
    57	        match term {
    58	            Term::Variant {
    59	                name,
    60	                module,
    61	                fields,
    62	                variable,
    63	            } => {
    64	                let is_defined_in_current_module = *module == self.current_module;
    65	                let is_internal = variable
    66	                    .type_
    67	                    .named_type_publicity()
    68	                    .unwrap_or(Publicity::Public)
    69	                    .is_internal();
    70	
    71	                // We don't want to expose information about an internal type,
    72	                // making it easy to rely on its internal structure.
    73	                // So what we do is we just show a catch all pattern `_` for
    74	                // those.
    75	                // We do this only if the internal type is defined in a
    76	                // different module from the one being analysed, otherwise it's
    77	                // totally fair to want to match on such type.
    78	                if is_internal && !is_defined_in_current_module {
    79	                    buffer.push('_');
    80	                    return;
    81	                }
    82	
    83	                let (module, name) = match self.names.named_constructor(module, name) {
    84	                    NameContextInformation::Qualified(module, name) => (Some(module), name),
    85	                    NameContextInformation::Unqualified(name) => (None, name),
    86	                    NameContextInformation::Unimported(module, name) => {
    87	                        (module.split('/').next_back(), name)
    88	                    }
    89	                };
    90	
    91	                if let Some(module) = module {
    92	                    buffer.push_str(module);
    93	                    buffer.push('.');
    94	                }
    95	                buffer.push_str(name);
    96	
    97	                if fields.is_empty() {
    98	                    return;
    99	                }
   100	                buffer.push('(');
   101	                for (i, field) in fields.iter().enumerate() {
   102	                    if i != 0 {
   103	                        buffer.push_str(", ");
   104	                    }
   105	
   106	                    let mut has_label = false;
   107	
   108	                    if let Some(label) = &field.label {
   109	                        buffer.push_str(label);
   110	                        buffer.push(':');
   111	                        has_label = true;
   112	                    }
   113	
   114	                    if let Some(&idx) = mapping.get(&field.variable.id) {
   115	                        let term = terms.get(idx).expect("Term must exist");
   116	
   117	                        match term {
   118	                            // If it is an infinite term and this field is labelled, it is generally
   119	                            // more useful to print just the label using label shorthand syntax.
   120	                            // For example, printing `Person(name:, age:)` instead of
   121	                            // `Person(name: _, age: _)`.
   122	                            Term::Infinite { .. } if has_label => {}
   123	                            Term::Infinite { .. }
   124	                            | Term::Variant { .. }
   125	                            | Term::Tuple { .. }
   126	                            | Term::EmptyList { .. }
   127	                            | Term::List { .. } => {
   128	                                // If this field has a label, the current buffer looks like `label:`,
   129	                                // so we want to print a space before printing the pattern for it.
   130	                                // If there is no label, we don't need to print the space.
   131	                                if has_label {
   132	                                    buffer.push(' ');
   133	                                }
   134	                                self.print(term, terms, mapping, buffer);
   135	                            }
   136	                        }
   137	                    } else if !has_label {
   138	                        buffer.push('_');
   139	                    }
   140	                }
   141	                buffer.push(')');
   142	            }
   143	            Term::Tuple { elements, .. } => {
   144	                buffer.push_str("#(");
   145	                for (i, variable) in elements.iter().enumerate() {
   146	                    if i != 0 {
   147	                        buffer.push_str(", ");
   148	                    }
   149	
   150	                    if let Some(&idx) = mapping.get(&variable.id) {
   151	                        self.print(
   152	                            terms.get(idx).expect("Term must exist"),
   153	                            terms,
   154	                            mapping,
   155	                            buffer,
   156	                        );
   157	                    } else {
   158	                        buffer.push('_');
   159	                    }
   160	                }
   161	                buffer.push(')');
   162	            }
   163	            Term::Infinite { .. } => buffer.push('_'),
   164	            Term::EmptyList { .. } => buffer.push_str("[]"),
   165	            Term::List { .. } => {
   166	                buffer.push('[');
   167	                self.print_list(term, terms, mapping, buffer);
   168	                buffer.push(']');
   169	            }
   170	        }
   171	    }
   172	
   173	    fn print_list(
   174	        &self,
   175	        term: &Term,
   176	        terms: &[Term],
   177	        mapping: &HashMap<usize, usize>,
   178	        buffer: &mut EcoString,
   179	    ) {
   180	        match term {
   181	            Term::Infinite { .. } | Term::Variant { .. } | Term::Tuple { .. } => buffer.push('_'),
   182	
   183	            Term::EmptyList { .. } => {}
   184	
   185	            Term::List { first, rest, .. } => {
   186	                if let Some(&idx) = mapping.get(&first.id) {
   187	                    self.print(
   188	                        terms.get(idx).expect("Term must exist"),
   189	                        terms,
   190	                        mapping,
   191	                        buffer,
   192	                    )
   193	                } else {
   194	                    buffer.push('_');
   195	                }
   196	
   197	                if let Some(&idx) = mapping.get(&rest.id) {
   198	                    let term = terms.get(idx).expect("Term must exist");
   199	
   200	                    match term {
   201	                        Term::EmptyList { .. } => {}
   202	                        Term::Variant { .. }
   203	                        | Term::Tuple { .. }
   204	                        | Term::Infinite { .. }
   205	                        | Term::List { .. } => {
   206	                            buffer.push_str(", ");
   207	                            self.print_list(term, terms, mapping, buffer)
   208	                        }
   209	                    }
   210	                } else {
   211	                    buffer.push_str(", ..");
   212	                }
   213	            }
   214	        }
   215	    }
   216	}

   252	        let mut mapping: HashMap<usize, usize> = HashMap::new();
   253	
   254	        for (index, term) in terms.iter().enumerate() {
   255	            _ = mapping.insert(term.variable().id, index);
   256	        }

   258	    }

    91	/// A small helper function to get the indentation at a given position.
    92	fn count_indentation(code: &str, line_numbers: &LineNumbers, line: u32) -> usize {
    93	    let mut indent_size = 0;
    94	    let line_start = *line_numbers
    95	        .line_starts
    96	        .get(line as usize)
    97	        .expect("Line number should be valid");
    98	
    99	    let mut chars = code[line_start as usize..].chars();
   100	    while chars.next() == Some(' ') {
   101	        indent_size += 1;
   102	    }
   103	
   104	    indent_size
   105	}
   106	
   107	/// Code action to remove literal tuples in case subjects, essentially making
   108	/// the elements of the tuples into the case's subjects.
   109	///
   110	/// The code action is only available for the i'th subject if:
   111	/// - it is a non-empty tuple, and
   112	/// - the i'th pattern (including alternative patterns) is a literal tuple for all clauses.
   113	///
   114	/// # Basic example:
   115	///
   116	/// The following case expression:
   117	///
   118	/// ```gleam
   119	/// case #(1, 2) {
   120	///     #(a, b) -> 0
   121	/// }
   122	/// ```
   123	///
   124	/// Becomes:
   125	///
   126	/// ```gleam
   127	/// case 1, 2 {
   128	///     a, b -> 0
   129	/// }
   130	/// ```
   131	///
   132	/// # Another example:
   133	///
   134	/// The following case expression does not produce any code action
   135	///
   136	/// ```gleam
   137	/// case #(1, 2) {
   138	///     a -> 0 // <- the pattern is not a tuple
   139	/// }
   140	/// ```
   141	pub struct RedundantTupleInCaseSubject<'a> {
   142	    edits: TextEdits<'a>,
   143	    code: &'a EcoString,
   144	    extra: &'a ModuleExtra,
   145	    params: &'a CodeActionParams,
   146	    module: &'a ast::TypedModule,
   147	    hovered: bool,
   148	}
   149	
   150	impl<'ast> ast::visit::Visit<'ast> for RedundantTupleInCaseSubject<'_> {
   151	    fn visit_typed_expr_case(
   152	        &mut self,
   153	        location: &'ast SrcSpan,
   154	        type_: &'ast Arc<Type>,
   155	        subjects: &'ast [TypedExpr],
   156	        clauses: &'ast [ast::TypedClause],
   157	        compiled_case: &'ast CompiledCase,
   158	    ) {
   159	        for (subject_idx, subject) in subjects.iter().enumerate() {
   160	            let TypedExpr::Tuple {
   161	                location, elements, ..
   162	            } = subject
   163	            else {
   164	                continue;
   165	            };
   166	
   167	            // Ignore empty tuple
   168	            if elements.is_empty() {
   169	                continue;
   170	            }
   171	
   172	            // We cannot rewrite clauses whose i-th pattern is not a discard or
   173	            // tuples.
   174	            let all_ith_patterns_are_tuples_or_discards = clauses
   175	                .iter()
   176	                .map(|clause| clause.pattern.get(subject_idx))
   177	                .all(|pattern| {
   178	                    matches!(
   179	                        pattern,
   180	                        Some(Pattern::Tuple { .. } | Pattern::Discard { .. })
   181	                    )
   182	                });
   183	
   184	            if !all_ith_patterns_are_tuples_or_discards {
   185	                continue;
   186	            }
   187	
   188	            self.delete_tuple_tokens(*location, elements.last().map(|element| element.location()));
   189	
   190	            for clause in clauses {
   191	                match clause.pattern.get(subject_idx) {
   192	                    Some(Pattern::Tuple { location, elements }) => self.delete_tuple_tokens(
   193	                        *location,
   194	                        elements.last().map(|element| element.location()),
   195	                    ),
   196	                    Some(Pattern::Discard { location, .. }) => {
   197	                        self.discard_tuple_items(*location, elements.len())
   198	                    }
   199	                    _ => panic!("safe: we've just checked all patterns must be discards/tuples"),
   200	                }
   201	            }
   202	            let range = self.edits.src_span_to_lsp_range(*location);
   203	            self.hovered = self.hovered || overlaps(self.params.range, range);
   204	        }
   205	
   206	        ast::visit::visit_typed_expr_case(self, location, type_, subjects, clauses, compiled_case)
   207	    }
   208	}
   209	
   210	impl<'a> RedundantTupleInCaseSubject<'a> {
   211	    pub fn new(
   212	        module: &'a Module,
   213	        line_numbers: &'a LineNumbers,
   214	        params: &'a CodeActionParams,
   215	    ) -> Self {
   216	        Self {
   217	            edits: TextEdits::new(line_numbers),
   218	            code: &module.code,
   219	            extra: &module.extra,
   220	            params,
   221	            module: &module.ast,
   222	            hovered: false,
   223	        }
   224	    }
   225	
   226	    pub fn code_actions(mut self) -> Vec<CodeAction> {
   227	        self.visit_typed_module(self.module);
   228	        if !self.hovered {
   229	            return vec![];
   230	        }
   231	
   232	        self.edits.edits.sort_by_key(|edit| edit.range.start);
   233	
   234	        let mut actions = vec![];
   235	        CodeActionBuilder::new("Remove redundant tuples")
   236	            .kind(CodeActionKind::REFACTOR_REWRITE)
   237	            .changes(self.params.text_document.uri.clone(), self.edits.edits)
   238	            .preferred(true)
   239	            .push_to(&mut actions);
   240	
   241	        actions
   242	    }
   243	
   244	    fn delete_tuple_tokens(&mut self, location: SrcSpan, last_elem_location: Option<SrcSpan>) {
   245	        let tuple_code = self
   246	            .code
   247	            .get(location.start as usize..location.end as usize)
   248	            .expect("valid span");
   249	
   250	        // Delete `#`
   251	        self.edits
   252	            .delete(SrcSpan::new(location.start, location.start + 1));
   253	
   254	        // Delete `(`
   255	        let (lparen_offset, _) = tuple_code
   256	            .match_indices('(')
   257	            // Ignore in comments
   258	            .find(|(i, _)| !self.extra.is_within_comment(location.start + *i as u32))
   259	            .expect("`(` not found in tuple");
   260	
   261	        self.edits.delete(SrcSpan::new(
   262	            location.start + lparen_offset as u32,
   263	            location.start + lparen_offset as u32 + 1,
   264	        ));
   265	
   266	        // Delete trailing `,` (if applicable)
   267	        if let Some(last_elem_location) = last_elem_location {
   268	            // Get the code after the last element until the tuple's `)`
   269	            let code_after_last_elem = self
   270	                .code
   271	                .get(last_elem_location.end as usize..location.end as usize)
   272	                .expect("valid span");
   273	
   274	            if let Some((trailing_comma_offset, _)) = code_after_last_elem
   275	                .rmatch_indices(',')
   276	                // Ignore in comments
   277	                .find(|(i, _)| {
   278	                    !self
   279	                        .extra
   280	                        .is_within_comment(last_elem_location.end + *i as u32)
   281	                })
   282	            {
   283	                self.edits.delete(SrcSpan::new(
   284	                    last_elem_location.end + trailing_comma_offset as u32,
   285	                    last_elem_location.end + trailing_comma_offset as u32 + 1,
   286	                ));
   287	            }
   288	        }
   289	
   290	        // Delete )
   291	        self.edits
   292	            .delete(SrcSpan::new(location.end - 1, location.end));
   293	    }
   294	
   295	    fn discard_tuple_items(&mut self, discard_location: SrcSpan, tuple_items: usize) {
   296	        // Replace the old discard with multiple discard, one for each of the
   297	        // tuple items.
   298	        self.edits.replace(
   299	            discard_location,
   300	            itertools::intersperse(iter::repeat_n("_", tuple_items), ", ").collect(),
   301	        )
   302	    }
   303	}
   304	
   305	/// Builder for code action to convert `let assert` into a case expression.
   306	///
   307	pub struct LetAssertToCase<'a> {
   308	    module: &'a Module,
   309	    params: &'a CodeActionParams,
   310	    actions: Vec<CodeAction>,
   311	    edits: TextEdits<'a>,
   312	}
   313	
   314	impl<'ast> ast::visit::Visit<'ast> for LetAssertToCase<'_> {
   315	    fn visit_typed_assignment(&mut self, assignment: &'ast TypedAssignment) {
   316	        let assignment_range = self.edits.src_span_to_lsp_range(assignment.location);
   317	        let assignment_start_range = self.edits.src_span_to_lsp_range(SrcSpan {
   318	            start: assignment.location.start,
   319	            end: assignment.value.location().start,
   320	        });
   321	        self.visit_typed_expr(&assignment.value);
   322	
   323	        // Only offer the code action if the cursor is over the statement and
   324	        // to prevent weird behaviour when `let assert` statements are nested,
   325	        // we only check for the code action between the `let` and `=`.
   326	        if !(within(self.params.range, assignment_range)
   327	            && overlaps(self.params.range, assignment_start_range))
   328	        {
   329	            return;
   330	        }
   331	
   332	        // This pattern only applies to `let assert`
   333	        let AssignmentKind::Assert { message, .. } = &assignment.kind else {
   334	            return;
   335	        };
   336	
   337	        // Get the source code for the tested expression
   338	        let location = assignment.value.location();
   339	        let expr = self
   340	            .module
   341	            .code
   342	            .get(location.start as usize..location.end as usize)
   343	            .expect("Location must be valid");
   344	
   345	        // Get the source code for the pattern
   346	        let pattern_location = assignment.pattern.location();
   347	        let pattern = self
   348	            .module
   349	            .code
   350	            .get(pattern_location.start as usize..pattern_location.end as usize)
   351	            .expect("Location must be valid");
   352	
   353	        let message = message.as_ref().map(|message| {
   354	            let location = message.location();
   355	            self.module
   356	                .code
   357	                .get(location.start as usize..location.end as usize)
   358	                .expect("Location must be valid")
   359	        });
   360	
   361	        let range = self.edits.src_span_to_lsp_range(assignment.location);
   362	
   363	        // Figure out which variables are assigned in the pattern
   364	        let variables = PatternVariableFinder::find_variables_in_pattern(&assignment.pattern);
   365	
   366	        let assigned = match variables.len() {
   367	            0 => "_",
   368	            1 => variables.first().expect("Variables is length one"),
   369	            _ => &format!("#({})", variables.join(", ")),
   370	        };
   371	
   372	        let mut new_text = format!("let {assigned} = ");
   373	        let panic_message = if let Some(message) = message {
   374	            &format!("panic as {message}")
   375	        } else {
   376	            "panic"
   377	        };
   378	        let clauses = vec![
   379	            // The existing pattern
   380	            CaseClause {
   381	                pattern,
   382	                // `_` is not a valid expression, so if we are not
   383	                // binding any variables in the pattern, we simply return Nil.
   384	                expression: if assigned == "_" { "Nil" } else { assigned },
   385	            },
   386	            CaseClause {
   387	                pattern: "_",
   388	                expression: panic_message,
   389	            },
   390	        ];
   391	        print_case_expression(range.start.character as usize, expr, clauses, &mut new_text);
   392	
   393	        let uri = &self.params.text_document.uri;
   394	
   395	        CodeActionBuilder::new("Convert to case")
   396	            .kind(CodeActionKind::REFACTOR_REWRITE)
   397	            .changes(uri.clone(), vec![TextEdit { range, new_text }])
   398	            .preferred(false)
   399	            .push_to(&mut self.actions);
   400	    }
   401	}
   402	
   403	impl<'a> LetAssertToCase<'a> {
   404	    pub fn new(
   405	        module: &'a Module,
   406	        line_numbers: &'a LineNumbers,
   407	        params: &'a CodeActionParams,
   408	    ) -> Self {
   409	        Self {
   410	            module,
   411	            params,
   412	            actions: Vec::new(),
   413	            edits: TextEdits::new(line_numbers),
   414	        }
   415	    }
   416	
   417	    pub fn code_actions(mut self) -> Vec<CodeAction> {
   418	        self.visit_typed_module(&self.module.ast);
   419	        self.actions
   420	    }
   421	}
   422	
   423	struct PatternVariableFinder {
   424	    pattern_variables: Vec<EcoString>,
   425	}
   426	
   427	impl PatternVariableFinder {
   428	    fn new() -> Self {
   429	        Self {
   430	            pattern_variables: Vec::new(),
   431	        }
   432	    }
   433	
   434	    fn find_variables_in_pattern(pattern: &TypedPattern) -> Vec<EcoString> {
   435	        let mut finder = Self::new();
   436	        finder.visit_typed_pattern(pattern);
   437	        finder.pattern_variables
   438	    }
   439	}

   441	impl<'ast> ast::visit::Visit<'ast> for PatternVariableFinder {
   442	    fn visit_typed_pattern_variable(
   443	        &mut self,
   444	        _location: &'ast SrcSpan,
   445	        name: &'ast EcoString,
   446	        _type: &'ast Arc<Type>,
   447	        _origin: &'ast VariableOrigin,
   448	    ) {
   449	        self.pattern_variables.push(name.clone());

   451

   454	        location: &'ast SrcSpan,

   463	        &mut self,
   464	        _location: &'ast SrcSpan,
   465	        _left_location: &'ast SrcSpan,
   466	        left_side_assignment: &'ast Option<(EcoString, SrcSpan)>,

   468	        _left_side_string: &'ast EcoString,

   471	        if let Some((name, _)) = left_side_assignment {
   472	            self.pattern_variables.push(name.clone());
   473	        }
   474	        if let AssignName::Variable(name) = right_side_assignment {
   475	            self.pattern_variables.push(name.clone());
   476	        }
   477	    }

  1203	
  1204	pub fn code_action_add_missing_patterns(
  1205	    module: &Module,
  1206	    line_numbers: &LineNumbers,
  1207	    params: &CodeActionParams,
  1208	    error: &Option<Error>,
  1209	    actions: &mut Vec<CodeAction>,
  1210	) {
  1211	    let uri = &params.text_document.uri;
  1212	    let Some(Error::Type { errors, .. }) = error else {
  1213	        return;
  1214	    };
  1215	    let missing_patterns = errors
  1216	        .iter()
  1217	        .filter_map(|error| {
  1218	            if let type_::Error::InexhaustiveCaseExpression { location, missing } = error {
  1219	                Some((*location, missing))
  1220	            } else {
  1221	                None
  1222	            }
  1223	        })
  1224	        .collect_vec();
  1225	
  1226	    if missing_patterns.is_empty() {
  1227	        return;
  1228	    }
  1229	
  1230	    for (location, missing) in missing_patterns {
  1231	        let mut edits = TextEdits::new(line_numbers);
  1232	        let range = edits.src_span_to_lsp_range(location);
  1233	        if !overlaps(params.range, range) {
  1234	            return;
  1235	        }
  1236	
  1237	        let Some(Located::Expression {
  1238	            expression: TypedExpr::Case {
  1239	                clauses, subjects, ..
  1240	            },
  1241	            ..
  1242	        }) = module.find_node(location.start)
  1243	        else {
  1244	            continue;
  1245	        };
  1246	
  1247	        let indent_size = count_indentation(&module.code, edits.line_numbers, range.start.line);
  1248	
  1249	        let indent = " ".repeat(indent_size);
  1250	
  1251	        // Insert the missing patterns just after the final clause, or just before
  1252	        // the closing brace if there are no clauses
  1253	
  1254	        let insert_at = clauses
  1255	            .last()
  1256	            .map(|clause| clause.location.end)
  1257	            .unwrap_or(location.end - 1);
  1258	
  1259	        for pattern in missing {
  1260	            let new_text = format!("\n{indent}  {pattern} -> todo");
  1261	            edits.insert(insert_at, new_text);
  1262	        }
  1263	
  1264	        // Add a newline + indent after the last pattern if there are no clauses
  1265	        //
  1266	        // This improves the generated code for this case:
  1267	        // ```gleam
  1268	        // case True {}
  1269	        // ```
  1270	        // This produces:
  1271	        // ```gleam
  1272	        // case True {
  1273	        //   True -> todo
  1274	        //   False -> todo
  1275	        // }
  1276	        // ```
  1277	        // Instead of:
  1278	        // ```gleam
  1279	        // case True {
  1280	        //   True -> todo
  1281	        //   False -> todo}
  1282	        // ```
  1283	        //
  1284	        if clauses.is_empty() {
  1285	            let last_subject_location = subjects
  1286	                .last()
  1287	                .expect("Case expressions have at least one subject")
  1288	                .location()
  1289	                .end;
  1290	
  1291	            // Find the opening brace of the case expression
  1292	            let chars = module.code[last_subject_location as usize..].chars();
  1293	            let mut start_brace_location = last_subject_location;
  1294	            for char in chars {
  1295	                start_brace_location += 1;
  1296	                if char == '{' {
  1297	                    break;
  1298	                }
  1299	            }
  1300	
  1301	            // Remove any blank spaces/lines between the start brace and end brace
  1302	            edits.delete(SrcSpan::new(start_brace_location, insert_at));
  1303	            edits.insert(insert_at, format!("\n{indent}"));
  1304	        }
  1305	
  1306	        CodeActionBuilder::new("Add missing patterns")
  1307	            .kind(CodeActionKind::QUICKFIX)
  1308	            .changes(uri.clone(), edits.edits)
  1309	            .preferred(true)
  1310	            .push_to(actions);
  1311	    }
  1312	}

  1318	    params: &'a CodeActionParams,

  1324	    fn visit_typed_assignment(&mut self, assignment: &'ast TypedAssignment) {
  1325	        self.visit_typed_expr(&assignment.value);
  1326	
  1327	        // We only offer this code action between `let` and `=`, because
  1328	        // otherwise it could lead to confusing behaviour if inside a block
  1329	        // which is part of a let binding.
  1330	        let pattern_location = assignment.pattern.location();

  1332	        let code_action_range = self.edits.src_span_to_lsp_range(location);
  1333	
  1334	        // Only offer the code action if the cursor is over the statement
  1335	        if !overlaps(code_action_range, self.params.range) {
  1336	            return;
  1337	        }
  1338	
  1339	        // We don't need to add an annotation if there already is one
  1340	        if assignment.annotation.is_some() {
  1341	            return;
  1342	        }
  1343	
  1344	        // Various expressions such as pipelines and `use` expressions generate assignments
  1345	        // internally. However, these cannot be annotated and so we don't offer a code action here.
  1346	        if matches!(assignment.kind, AssignmentKind::Generated) {
  1347	            return;
  1348	        }
  1349

Now I see the issue! The "Add missing patterns" code action is inserting missing patterns. But let me understand the PR description better. The issue is that when you have a case expression with comments inside (like `// wibble wobble`), the "Add missing patterns" code action removes those comments.

Let me look at the code more carefully, particularly lines 1251-1304. The key issue seems to be around line 1284-1303, where if there are no clauses, it deletes everything between the opening brace and the insertion point. But there's also the case where there ARE clauses - the missing patterns are inserted after the last clause.

But the PR description says:
```
pub fn main() -> Nil {
  case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
  }
}
```

This is a case with NO clauses (just a comment). When "Add missing patterns" is triggered, it should preserve the comment.

Let me look at what happens when `clauses.is_empty()`: the code on lines 1284-1303 deletes everything between the opening brace and the `insert_at` (which is `location.end - 1`, the position before the closing `}`). This would delete the comment.

But wait, the issue might also be about the case where there ARE clauses with comments. Let me check how `insert_at` is determined when there are clauses. `insert_at = clauses.last().map(|clause| clause.location.end).unwrap_or(location.end - 1);` - so comments after the last clause but before `}` would be preserved? Actually no, the insert happens AFTER the last clause, which would be before the closing `}`. If there were comments between the last clause and `}`, they'd be preserved because the new patterns are inserted at `clause.location.end`.

Actually, wait. Let me re-read the PR. The example shows:

```gleam
pub fn main() -> Nil {
  case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
  }
}
```

This has NO clauses. So `clauses.is_empty()` is true, and `insert_at = location.end - 1`. Then the code at lines 1284-1303 deletes everything between the opening brace and `insert_at`:

```
edits.delete(SrcSpan::new(start_brace_location, insert_at));
```

This would delete the comment `// wibble wobble`! 

But also, even when there ARE clauses, if there are comments after the last clause, they could be affected because `insert_at` is after the last clause. The new patterns would be inserted before the comments. But wait, the comments would be preserved in that case.

Actually, the problem is more subtle. Let me think about a case with clauses AND comments:

```gleam
case x {
  Some(x) -> x
  // wibble wobble
}
```

Here, the comment is after `Some(x) -> x` but before `}`. The `insert_at` would be the end of the last clause (`Some(x) -> x`), so new patterns would be inserted after that clause but before the comment. The comment would be preserved. But wait, the comment is inside the case block, between the last clause and `}`. Is there a possibility that comments get removed?

    47	fn apply_code_action(title: &str, tester: TestProject<'_>, range: Range) -> String {
    48	    let titles = vec![title];
    49	    let changes = actions_with_title(titles, &tester, range)
    50	        .pop()
    51	        .expect("No action with the given title")
    52	        .edit
    53	        .expect("No workspace edit found")
    54	        .changes
    55	        .expect("No text edit found");
    56	    apply_code_edit(tester, changes)
    57	}

    59	fn apply_code_edit(
    60	    tester: TestProject<'_>,
    61	    changes: HashMap<Url, Vec<lsp_types::TextEdit>>,
    62	) -> String {
    63	    let mut changed_files: HashMap<Url, String> = HashMap::new();
    64	    for (uri, change) in changes {
    65	        let code = match changed_files.get(&uri) {
    66	            Some(code) => code,
    67	            None => tester
    68	                .src_from_module_url(&uri)
    69	                .unwrap_or_else(|| panic!("no src for url {uri:?}")),
    70	        };
    71	        let code = super::apply_code_edit(code, change);
    72	        let _ = changed_files.insert(uri, code);
    73	    }
    74	
    75	    show_code_edits(tester, changed_files)
    76	}
    77	
    78	fn show_code_edits(tester: TestProject<'_>, changed_files: HashMap<Url, String>) -> String {
    79	    let format_code = |url: &Url, code: &String| {
    80	        format!(
    81	            "// --- Edits applied to module '{}'\n{}",
    82	            tester.module_name_from_url(url).expect("a module"),
    83	            code
    84	        )
    85	    };
    86	
    87	    // If the file that changed is the main one we just show its code.
    88	    if changed_files.len() == 1 {
    89	        let mut changed = changed_files.iter().peekable();
    90	        let (url, code) = changed.peek().unwrap();
    91	        if tester.module_name_from_url(url) == Some("app".into()) {
    92	            code.to_string()
    93	        } else {
    94	            format_code(url, code)
    95	        }
    96	    } else {
    97	        // If more than a single file changed we want to add the name of the
    98	        // file before each!
    99	        changed_files
   100	            .iter()
   101	            .map(|(url, code)| format_code(url, code))
   102	            .join("\n")
   103	    }
   104	}

The issue is in lines 1251-1304. Let me re-read them carefully:\n\n```rust\n// Insert the missing patterns just after the final clause, or just before\n// the closing brace if there are no clauses\n\nlet insert_at = clauses\n    .last()\n    .map(|clause| clause.location.end)\n    .unwrap_or(location.end - 1);\n\nfor pattern in missing {\n    let new_text = format!("\\n{indent}  {pattern} -> todo");\n    edits.insert(insert_at, new_text);\n}\n\n// Add a newline + indent after the last pattern if there are no clauses\n//\n// This improves the generated code for this case:\n// ```gleam\n// case True {}\n// ```\n// This produces:\n// ```gleam\n// case True {\n//   True -> todo\n//   False -> todo\n// }\n// ```\n// Instead of:\n// ```gleam\n// case True {\n//   True -> todo\n//   False -> todo}\n// ```\n//\nif clauses.is_empty() {\n    let last_subject_location = subjects\n        .last()\n        .expect("Case expressions have at least one subject")\n        .location()\n        .end;\n\n    // Find the opening brace of the case expression\n    let chars = module.code[last_subject_location as usize..].chars();\n    let mut start_brace_location = last_subject_location;\n    for char in chars {\n        start_brace_location += 1;\n        if char == \'{\' {\n            break;\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Remove any blank spaces/lines between the start brace and end brace\n    edits.delete(SrcSpan::new(start_brace_location, insert_at));\n    edits.insert(insert_at, format!("\\n{indent}"));\n}\n```\n\nSo when there are no clauses, it:\n1. Sets `insert_at = location.end - 1` (just before the closing `}`)\n2. Inserts missing patterns at `insert_at`\n3. Then deletes everything between `{` and `insert_at` (which includes any comments)\n4. Then inserts a newline+indent at `insert_at`\n\nThe problem is step 3: it deletes everything between the opening brace and `insert_at`, which includes any comments. 2026-05-30 18:37:52,850 - INFO - swea-agent-gleam-lang__gleam-5532 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now let me look at the key part of the `code_action_add_missing_patterns` function again. The issue is in lines 1251-1304. Let me re-read them carefully:

```rust
// Insert the missing patterns just after the final clause, or just before
// the closing brace if there are no clauses

let insert_at = clauses
    .last()
    .map(|clause| clause.location.end)
    .unwrap_or(location.end - 1);

for pattern in missing {
    let new_text = format!("\n{indent}  {pattern} -> todo");
    edits.insert(insert_at, new_text);
}

// Add a newline + indent after the last pattern if there are no clauses
//
// This improves the generated code for this case:
// ```gleam
// case True {}
// ```
// This produces:
// ```gleam
// case True {
//   True -> todo
//   False -> todo
// }
// ```
// Instead of:
// ```gleam
// case True {
//   True -> todo
//   False -> todo}
// ```
//
if clauses.is_empty() {
    let last_subject_location = subjects
        .last()
        .expect("Case expressions have at least one subject")
        .location()
        .end;

    // Find the opening brace of the case expression
    let chars = module.code[last_subject_location as usize..].chars();
    let mut start_brace_location = last_subject_location;
    for char in chars {
        start_brace_location += 1;
        if char == '{' {
            break;
        }
    }

    // Remove any blank spaces/lines between the start brace and end brace
    edits.delete(SrcSpan::new(start_brace_location, insert_at));
    edits.insert(insert_at, format!("\n{indent}"));
}
```

So when there are no clauses, it:
1. Sets `insert_at = location.end - 1` (just before the closing `}`)
2. Inserts missing patterns at `insert_at`
3. Then deletes everything between `{` and `insert_at` (which includes any comments)
4. Then inserts a newline+indent at `insert_at`

The problem is step 3: it deletes everything between the opening brace and `insert_at`, which includes any comments. The fix should preserve comments.

But also, when there ARE clauses, the `insert_at` is after the last clause. If there are comments after the last clause but before `}`, the new patterns would be inserted before those comments. That seems fine - comments would be preserved.

However, the PR description specifically mentions this case:

```gleam
pub fn main() -> Nil {
  case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
  }
}
```

This has no clauses. The comment `// wibble wobble` is between `{` and `}`. The code deletes everything between `{` and `insert_at` (which is just before `}`), thus removing the comment.

Let me think about the fix. Instead of deleting everything between `{` and the closing `}`, we should only remove blank spaces/lines and preserve comments. But actually, looking at the code again, the deletion happens BEFORE the insertion (line 1302), but the insertion happens at line 1261. Wait, let me re-read...

Actually, looking at the order:
1. Lines 1259-1262: Insert missing patterns at `insert_at`
2. Lines 1284-1303: If clauses.is_empty(), delete everything between `{` and `insert_at`, then insert a newline+indent at `insert_at`

But `insert_at` is `location.end - 1` when `clauses.is_empty()`. So:
- First, patterns are inserted at the position before `}`
- Then, everything between `{` and `insert_at` is deleted

This seems wrong! The patterns that were just inserted would be deleted too because they're between `{` and `}`. But wait, `edits` uses a specific ordering... Let me look at how edits are applied.

   842	    let mut result = src.to_string();
   843	    let line_numbers = LineNumbers::new(src);
   844	    let mut offset = 0;
   845	
   846	    change.sort_by_key(|edit| (edit.range.start.line, edit.range.start.character));

Let me look at the `code_action_add_missing_patterns` function one more time and think about what the fix should be.

The core issue: when `clauses.is_empty()`, the code deletes everything between `{` and `}` (line 1302). This removes comments. 

The fix should be: instead of deleting everything between `{` and `}`, we should only clean up whitespace and preserve comments. But actually, a simpler fix would be: if there are comments or non-whitespace content between `{` and `}`, we should not delete them. Or better: we should just not do the delete at all when there's non-whitespace content.

But wait, let me also think about the case with clauses. The PR description says:

> I commented out the old variant code paths so I could copy paste some of the code accordingly in the new ones, but the code action removed the comments.

This could also apply to cases where there ARE clauses. For example:

```gleam

  Some(x) -> x
  // Old code:
  // None -> todo
}
```

In this case, `clauses` is not empty (there's one clause `Some(x) -> x`). `insert_at` would be the end of the last clause (`Some(x) -> x`). The new patterns would be inserted after that clause but before the comments. The comments would be preserved. So this case is fine.

```gleam
case x {
  // Old code:
  // Some(x) -> x
}
```

Here `clauses` is empty (no actual clauses, just comments). `insert_at = location.end - 1`. Then the delete would remove the comments.

Actually, looking more carefully, I think the fix should be to only delete if the content between `{` and `}` is purely whitespace. Let me write the fix.

    .last()

When there are clauses, `insert_at` is after the last clause. New patterns are inserted there. If there are comments between the last clause and `}`, the new patterns go before those comments. The comments are preserved. But they might now be in an odd position (between the new patterns and `}`). However, that's probably acceptable.

```rust

        .last()
        .expect("Case expressions have at least one subject")
        .location()
        .end;

2026-05-30 18:40:48,711 - INFO - swea-agent-gleam-lang__gleam-5532 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now, let me think about the fix more carefully. The issue is that the delete operation removes comments. The simplest fix is to check if the content between `{` and `}` is only whitespace, and if not, skip the delete or only delete leading/trailing whitespace.

But actually, I think the proper fix is different. Let me re-examine the code:

The code does:
1. Insert missing patterns at `insert_at`
2. If no clauses, delete from `{` to `insert_at` and insert a newline

But step 2 deletes things between `{` and `}`, including the patterns that were just inserted in step 1 (since they're at `insert_at` which is within the delete range). So after the delete, the patterns are gone, and then the newline is added.

Wait, but the edit application handles offsets. Let me trace through with the `apply_code_edit` function:

```rust
pub fn apply_code_edit(src: &str, mut change: Vec<lsp_types::TextEdit>) -> String {
    let mut result = src.to_string();
    let line_numbers = LineNumbers::new(src);
    let mut offset = 0;

    change.sort_by_key(|edit| (edit.range.start.line, edit.range.start.character));
    for edit in change {
        let start = line_numbers.byte_index(edit.range.start) as i32 - offset;
        let end = line_numbers.byte_index(edit.range.end) as i32 - offset;
        let range = (start as usize)..(end as usize);
        offset += end - start;
        offset -= edit.new_text.len() as i32;
        result.replace_range(range, &edit.new_text);
    }

    result
}
```

This is the test helper. The actual LSP code might work differently. But for understanding the intended behavior, let me trace through a simple example:

Source: `case bool {}` (let's say it's `case bool {\n}`)

Actually, let me just look at what the snapshot shows. For `case bool {}`:
- Input: `pub fn main(bool: Bool) {\n  case bool {}\n}\n`
- Output: `pub fn main(bool: Bool) {\n  case bool {\n    True -> todo\n    False -> todo\n  }\n}\n`

So the `{}` (empty braces) becomes `{\n    True -> todo\n    False -> todo\n  }`. The patterns are inserted and properly formatted.

Now for the bug case:
- Input: `pub fn main() -> Nil {\n  case [] {\n    \n    // wibble wobble\n  }\n}\n`
- Expected output: The patterns should be added while preserving the comment.
- Actual output (likely): The comment is removed.

Let me now look at how the code handles this. The key is the delete on line 1302:

```rust
edits.delete(SrcSpan::new(start_brace_location, insert_at));
```

For the bug case, `start_brace_location` is the position after `{` and `insert_at` is `location.end - 1` (before `}`). So it deletes everything between `{` and `}`, which includes the comment.

The fix: instead of deleting everything, we should only delete if the content is purely whitespace. Or better, we should not delete at all and instead insert the patterns in a smarter way.

Actually, thinking about it more, I think the best fix is:

When `clauses.is_empty()`, we should find the position right after `{` (which is `start_brace_location`) and insert the patterns there, and then ensure there's a newline before `}`. But we should NOT delete existing content (like comments).

Wait, let me reconsider the design. The purpose of the delete is:
1. If `case True {}`, we want to produce:
```
case True {
  True -> todo
  False -> todo
}
```
Instead of:
```
case True {
  True -> todo
  False -> todo}
```

The delete removes the empty space between `{` and `}` so the closing brace is properly placed after the patterns.

If there are comments, we shouldn't delete them. We should insert the patterns and keep the comments. The comments would be between the patterns and the closing brace, or before the patterns.

So the fix: check if the content between `{` and `insert_at` is only whitespace. If it is, do the delete (as before). If it's not (i.e., there are comments or other non-whitespace content), skip the delete and just insert the patterns at `insert_at`.

But wait, if we insert at `insert_at` (which is `location.end - 1`, just before `}`), and there's a comment before `}`, the patterns would be inserted after the comment. That might look odd but it preserves the comment.

Actually, I think a better approach would be:
- Find the position right after `{` (let's call it `after_brace`)
- Check if the content between `after_brace` and `insert_at` is only whitespace
- If yes, do the current behavior (delete + insert newline)
- If no, insert patterns at `insert_at` without deleting anything

But there's another issue: when `clauses.is_empty()` and there IS content (comments), the insert_at is `location.end - 1`. The patterns are inserted before `}`, after the comments. That's fine.

Let me now implement the fix.

Let me instead look at what the actual issue is more carefully by examining the code logic and writing a proper fix.

The issue is in lines 1284-1304. When `clauses.is_empty()`:
1. Find start_brace_location (position after `{`)
2. Delete everything from after `{` to `insert_at` (just before `}`)
3. Insert newline+indent

Step 2 removes comments. The fix should preserve comments.

The simplest fix: check if the content between `start_brace_location` and `insert_at` is only whitespace. If it is, do the current behavior. If not, skip the delete and just ensure there's a proper newline before `}`.

But actually, I think an even simpler fix is: instead of deleting everything and inserting a newline, we should just not do the delete if there's non-whitespace content. Or better, we should only trim the whitespace but preserve comments.

Let me look at what content is between `start_brace_location` and `insert_at`:

For `case [] {\n    \n    // wibble wobble\n  }`:
- Between `{` and `}`: `\n    \n    // wibble wobble\n  `
- This contains non-whitespace (the comment)

The current code deletes all of this. Then inserts `\n{indent}`. The patterns would be inserted at `insert_at` (before `}`), but since the delete happens first (due to sorting), the patterns are inserted after the delete. Wait, I showed earlier that the delete and inserts happen at the same position...

Actually wait, for this case:
- `start_brace_location` = position after `{` 
- `insert_at` = position of `}`

These are different positions when there's content between them. The delete range is `(start_brace_location, insert_at)`. The inserts are at `insert_at`.

After sorting: delete (start_brace_location, insert_at) comes first because start_brace_location < insert_at. Then inserts at insert_at happen.

So the delete removes everything between `{` and `}`, including the comment. Then the patterns are inserted at `insert_at` (which is now at a different position due to offset adjustments). But the comment is gone!

The fix: we should check if there's any non-whitespace content between `start_brace_location` and `insert_at`. If there is, we should NOT delete it.

Let me implement this fix:

But wait, I need to also check: what happens when there ARE clauses but there are comments after the last clause? Let me re-examine that scenario.

When there ARE clauses:
- `insert_at = clauses.last().unwrap().location.end` (position after last clause)
- Patterns are inserted at `insert_at`
- No delete happens

So if there's a comment after the last clause, the patterns are inserted before the comment. The comment is preserved. That should be fine.

But what about this edge case: what if the case has clauses but the `case` is still inexhaustive? Like:

```gleam
case x {
  // Comment
  Some(x) -> x
}
```

Here `clauses` has one clause (`Some(x) -> x`), and `insert_at` is the end of that clause. The new pattern would be inserted after `Some(x) -> x`, before `}` and after the comment. The comment before the first clause is preserved. Good.

But wait, there's another scenario: what if there are comments but no clauses, and the `between.trim().is_empty()` check... Actually, `trim()` removes whitespace but NOT comments. A comment like `// wibble wobble` is not whitespace, so `between.trim().is_empty()` would be false, and we'd skip the delete. 

But what about the case where there are only blank lines (no comments)? `between.trim().is_empty()` would be true, and we'd do the delete. That's the correct behavior.

Now let me think about edge cases:
1. `case [] {}` - no clauses, no content between braces → `between.trim().is_empty()` = true → delete happens → works as before
2. `case [] {\n    \n    // wibble wobble\n  }` - no clauses, comment between braces → `between.trim().is_empty()` = false → skip delete → patterns inserted before `}`, comment preserved
3. `case [] {\n    \n  }` - no clauses, only whitespace → `between.trim().is_empty()` = true → delete happens → works as before

Case 2 is the fix for the bug. But wait, what does the output look like for case 2?

Currently with my fix:
- `insert_at = location.end - 1` (just before `}`)
- Patterns inserted at `insert_at`
- Since `between.trim().is_empty()` is false, skip delete

So the patterns are inserted just before `}`. The result would be:
```gleam
case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
  True -> todo
  False -> todo
  }
```

That's not great formatting. The patterns should be indented properly. Let me check what `indent` is:

```rust
let indent_size = count_indentation(&module.code, edits.line_numbers, range.start.line);
let indent = " ".repeat(indent_size);
```

So `indent` is the indentation of the `case` line. Then patterns are inserted with `{indent}  {pattern} -> todo`. So:

```gleam
pub fn main() -> Nil {
  case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
    True -> todo
    False -> todo
  }
}
```

Wait, the patterns would be inserted at `insert_at` which is just before `}`. The patterns include `\n` at the beginning:
```rust
let new_text = format!("\n{indent}  {pattern} -> todo");
```

So they'd be:
```
\n  True -> todo
\n  False -> todo
```

Inserted just before `}`. So:
```
  case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
  True -> todo
  False -> todo
  }
```

Hmm, but there's already a newline before `}` from the original code (`\n  }`). So inserting `\n  True -> todo\n  False -> todo` before `}` gives:

```
  case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
  True -> todo
  False -> todo
  }
```

But the comment `// wibble wobble` is before the patterns. The patterns appear after the comment and before `}`. The formatting might look a bit odd (comment before new patterns) but at least the comment is preserved, which is what the PR wants.

However, I think a better approach would be to insert the patterns AFTER the `{` (or after the existing content), preserving the relative order. But actually, the current approach (insert before `}`) seems fine for preserving comments. The comment was there before, and it stays there. New patterns are added after it.

But wait, there's another issue: when there are clauses but there are comments AFTER the last clause, the new patterns are inserted before those comments. That could be confusing. But the PR description only mentions the case of no clauses with comments.

Let me also think about whether my fix handles the case where there are multiple comments correctly. The `between.trim().is_empty()` check works for any content - if there's any non-whitespace (including comments), we skip the delete.

Now, let me also consider: what if the case has content like `case [] {\n  // comment\n}`? In this case, `between.trim()` would be `// comment` which is not empty, so we skip the delete. The patterns would be inserted before `}`. The result:

```
case [] {
  // comment
  True -> todo
  False -> todo
}
```

That looks reasonable. The comment is preserved.

But what if the content is just spaces and newlines? `between.trim().is_empty()` = true, so we delete and insert properly.

Let me now also check if there's a case where the `between` slice could be empty or cause issues. If `start_brace_location` > `insert_at`, the slice would panic. But `start_brace_location` is always <= `insert_at` because:
- `start_brace_location` is after `{`
- `insert_at` is `location.end - 1` (the position of `}`)
- `{` comes before `}` in source, so `start_brace_location` <= `insert_at`

Actually, there's a subtle case: `start_brace_location` could equal `insert_at` (like `case bool {}`). In that case, `between` is an empty string slice, and `trim().is_empty()` is true. So the delete is `(start_brace_location, insert_at)` which is an empty range. That's fine.

Now, I should also think about whether the comment preservation also needs to work when there ARE clauses. Let me re-read the PR description:

> I refactored some code and wanted to generate the correct variants in an outdated case statements.
> I commented out the old variant code paths so I could copy paste some of the code accordingly in the new ones, but the code action removed the comments.

The example shows:
```gleam
pub fn main() -> Nil {
  case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
  }
}
```

This has NO clauses. The comment represents an old commented-out pattern. The user triggers "Add missing patterns" and the comment is removed.

My fix addresses this by not deleting the content between `{` and `}` when there's non-whitespace content.

But what about this scenario:
```gleam
case x {
  Some(x) -> x
  // None -> todo  (old code, commented out)
}
```

Here there IS a clause (`Some(x) -> x`). The comment is after the last clause. The current code would:
- `insert_at = end of Some(x) -> x`
- Insert new patterns after `Some(x) -> x` but before the comment

So the comment would be preserved (it stays after the new patterns). That seems fine.

But what about:
```gleam
case x {
  // Some(x) -> x  (old code, commented out)
}
```

This has no clauses again. My fix handles this.

What about:
```gleam
case x {
  // Old pattern
  // Some(x) -> x
  None -> todo
}
```

Here there IS a clause (`None -> todo`). The comments are before the first clause. The `insert_at` would be after `None -> todo`. New patterns would be inserted after `None -> todo`, preserving the comments before it. That's fine.

So my fix should address the main issue. But let me think if there are any other places where comments could be removed...

Actually, wait. Let me re-read the code for the case where there ARE clauses:

```rust
let insert_at = clauses
    .last()
    .map(|clause| clause.location.end)
    .unwrap_or(location.end - 1);

for pattern in missing {
    let new_text = format!("\n{indent}  {pattern} -> todo");
    edits.insert(insert_at, new_text);
}
```

If there's a clause and there's a comment between that clause and `}`, the patterns are inserted at the end of the clause, which is before the comment. So the comment is preserved. Good.

But what if the comment is BEFORE the first clause? Like:
```gleam
case x {
  // Some(x) -> x
  None -> todo
}
```

`clauses` would have one clause (`None -> todo`). `insert_at` is the end of `None -> todo`. Patterns are inserted after `None -> todo`, preserving the comment before it. Good.

So my fix should be sufficient.

   480	pub fn code_action_inexhaustive_let_to_case(
   481	    module: &Module,
   482	    line_numbers: &LineNumbers,
   483	    params: &CodeActionParams,
   484	    error: &Option<Error>,
   485	    actions: &mut Vec<CodeAction>,
   486	) {
   487	    let Some(Error::Type { errors, .. }) = error else {
   488	        return;
   489	    };
   490	    let inexhaustive_assignments = errors
   491	        .iter()
   492	        .filter_map(|error| {
   493	            if let type_::Error::InexhaustiveLetAssignment { location, missing } = error {
   494	                Some((*location, missing))
   495	            } else {
   496	                None
   497	            }
   498	        })
   499	        .collect_vec();
   500	
   501	    if inexhaustive_assignments.is_empty() {
   502	        return;
   503	    }
   504	
   505	    for (location, missing) in inexhaustive_assignments {
   506	        let mut text_edits = TextEdits::new(line_numbers);
   507	
   508	        let range = text_edits.src_span_to_lsp_range(location);
   509	        if !overlaps(params.range, range) {
   510	            return;
   511	        }
   512	
   513	        let Some(Located::Statement(TypedStatement::Assignment(assignment))) =
   514	            module.find_node(location.start)
   515	        else {
   516	            continue;
   517	        };
   518	
   519	        let TypedAssignment {
   520	            value,
   521	            pattern,
   522	            kind: AssignmentKind::Let,
   523	            location,
   524	            compiled_case: _,
   525	            annotation: _,
   526	        } = assignment.as_ref()
   527	        else {
   528	            continue;
   529	        };
   530	
   531	        // Get the source code for the tested expression
   532	        let value_location = value.location();
   533	        let expr = module
   534	            .code
   535	            .get(value_location.start as usize..value_location.end as usize)
   536	            .expect("Location must be valid");
   537	
   538	        // Get the source code for the pattern
   539	        let pattern_location = pattern.location();
   540	        let pattern_code = module
   541	            .code
   542	            .get(pattern_location.start as usize..pattern_location.end as usize)
   543	            .expect("Location must be valid");
   544	
   545	        let range = text_edits.src_span_to_lsp_range(*location);
   546	
   547	        // Figure out which variables are assigned in the pattern
   548	        let variables = PatternVariableFinder::find_variables_in_pattern(pattern);
   549	
   550	        let assigned = match variables.len() {
   551	            0 => "_",
   552	            1 => variables.first().expect("Variables is length one"),
   553	            _ => &format!("#({})", variables.join(", ")),
   554	        };
   555	
   556	        let mut new_text = format!("let {assigned} = ");
   557	        print_case_expression(
   558	            range.start.character as usize,
   559	            expr,
   560	            iter::once(CaseClause {
   561	                pattern: pattern_code,
   562	                expression: if assigned == "_" { "Nil" } else { assigned },
   563	            })
   564	            .chain(missing.iter().map(|pattern| CaseClause {
   565	                pattern,
   566	                expression: "todo",
   567	            }))
   568	            .collect(),
   569	            &mut new_text,
   570	        );
   571	
   572	        let uri = &params.text_document.uri;
   573	
   574	        text_edits.replace(*location, new_text);
   575	
   576	        CodeActionBuilder::new("Convert to case")
   577	            .kind(CodeActionKind::QUICKFIX)
   578	            .changes(uri.clone(), text_edits.edits)
   579	            .preferred(true)
   580	            .push_to(actions);
   581	    }
   582	}

The logic works correctly:
- Empty/whitespace → `trim().is_empty()` = true → delete happens (existing behavior)
- Comment → `trim().is_empty()` = false → skip delete (preserving comments)

Now, I'm thinking about another edge case. What if there's a comment that uses `/* */` style? But Gleam doesn't have block comments, only line comments (`//`). So that's fine.

What if there's a string literal that looks like a comment? The content between `{` and `}` in a case expression wouldn't contain string literals that look like comments. Comments are `//` and they're clearly comments.

Now, I think my fix is complete. But let me also consider: should we also handle the case where there ARE clauses but there are comments after the last clause? Let me think about this more carefully.

Current behavior when there are clauses:
- `insert_at = end of last clause`
- Patterns inserted at `insert_at`
- If there's a comment after the last clause, patterns go before the comment

This preserves the comment. So it's fine.

But what about when there are clauses and we want to insert patterns, and there's a comment BEFORE the first clause? Like:

```gleam
case x {
  // TODO: handle this
  Some(x) -> x
}
```

Here `clauses` = `[Some(x) -> x]`. `insert_at` = end of `Some(x) -> x`. Patterns are inserted after `Some(x) -> x`. The comment before `Some(x)` is preserved. Good.

So my fix addresses the specific issue in the PR description. Let me also think about whether we need to handle the case where there are clauses and comments exist between the last clause and `}`. Currently, patterns are inserted before such comments. This is acceptable behavior.

But actually, wait. I just realized something. Let me look at the code more carefully for the case when there ARE clauses. The `insert_at` is `clause.location.end`. But what if there are multiple clauses? It's the last clause. What if the last clause has a comment after it on the same line? Like:

```gleam
case x {
  Some(x) -> x // handle some
}
```

The `clause.location.end` would be the end of the whole clause, which includes the comment? Let me check...

Actually, `clause.location` spans the entire clause including the body expression. But the comment might be part of the body or after it. I'm not sure if the AST includes comments in spans. Typically, AST spans don't include comments that come after the expression. So `clause.location.end` would be the end of the body expression, not including the comment.

So `insert_at` would be after the body expression but before the comment. New patterns would be inserted before the comment. The comment would be preserved.

This all seems fine.

Now, I'm going to also check if there's a need to handle the "Add missing patterns" for the case when `clauses` is empty but there are multiple subjects (like `case a, b {}`). The `add_missing_patterns_multi` test already covers this and passes.

Let me also think about whether my change could cause any issues with the edit application. The `edits.delete` and `edits.insert` are added to the same list. When `between.trim().is_empty()` is false, we skip both the delete and the insert of `\n{indent}`. The patterns were already inserted at `insert_at` (just before `}`). So the result would be:

For `case [] {\n    \n    // wibble wobble\n  }`:
- Patterns inserted at `insert_at` (before `}`)
- No delete, no extra newline

Result:
```
case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
  True -> todo
  False -> todo
  }
```

The `}` stays on its original line. The patterns are properly indented. The comment is preserved. This seems acceptable.

But wait, there's a formatting issue: the patterns include `\n{indent}  ` prefix. So they start at the right indentation. But the `}` already has a newline before it. Let me trace:

Original: `...{\n    \n    // wibble wobble\n  }`

`insert_at` is the position of `}` (let's call it position P).

Pattern 1: insert `\n  True -> todo` at P.
String becomes: `...{\n    \n    // wibble wobble\n  True -> todo}`

Pattern 2: insert `\n  False -> todo` at P.
String becomes: `...{\n    \n    // wibble wobble\n  True -> todo\n  False -> todo}`

So the final result is:
```
case [] {
    
    // wibble wobble
  True -> todo
  False -> todo
  }
```

Wait, the `}` was at the end. After inserting patterns before `}`, the `}` is now on the same line as the last pattern? Actually no, `\n  False -> todo` includes `\n` at the start, so there's a newline before `False -> todo`. But the `}` was originally preceded by `\n  ` (newline + 2 spaces). The patterns are inserted BEFORE `}`, so they go before the `\n  }` part. Let me re-trace:

Original string (with positions):

Let me now summarize what I've done:

## Summary

The issue was that the "Add missing patterns" code action was removing comments inside `case` statements when there were no clauses.

The problem was in the `code_action_add_missing_patterns` function in `/testbed/language-server/src/code_action.rs`. When a case expression has no clauses (e.g., `case [] { /* comment */ }`), the code was:
1. Finding the opening brace `{` position
2. Deleting everything between `{` and the closing `}` position
3. Inserting a newline before `}`

This deleted any comments or other content inside the case body.

My fix:
1. Check if the content between the opening brace and the insertion point is purely whitespace (using `trim().is_empty()`)
2. If it is whitespace-only, use the original behavior (delete everything, insert newline)
3. If there's non-whitespace content (like comments), preserve it by only removing trailing whitespace before the closing brace, and then inserting the proper newline

This ensures that:
- Comments inside empty case statements are preserved
- The formatting still works correctly (the `}` is properly positioned after the new patterns)
- Existing behavior for empty/whitespace-only case bodies is unchanged</think>Let me verify the fix by looking at the final state of the changed

+                // brace is properly positioned.

-            edits.insert(insert_at, format!("\n{indent}"));
+            // Get the content between the opening brace and the position where
+            // we're going to insert the missing patterns
+            let between = &module.code
+                [start_brace_location as usize..insert_at as usize];
+
+            // Only remove blank spaces/lines between the start brace and end
+            // brace if there are no comments or other non-whitespace content
+            if between.trim().is_empty() {
+                edits.delete(SrcSpan::new(start_brace_location, insert_at));
+                edits.insert(insert_at, format!("\n{indent}"));
+            } else {
+                // When there is non-whitespace content (like comments), we
+                // need to preserve it. We remove any trailing whitespace
+                // before the closing brace and add a newline so the closing
+                // brace is properly positioned.
+                let trimmed_end = between.trim_end();
+                let trailing_whitespace_len =
+                    (between.len() - trimmed_end.len()) as u32;
+                let trailing_start = insert_at - trailing_whitespace_len;
+                edits.delete(SrcSpan::new(trailing_start, insert_at));
+                edits.insert(insert_at, format!("\n{indent}"));
+            }
         }
